  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_f14db393-ad73-4396-b108-badd811d9fc7'
      });

<a href="/questions/454857-what-kind-of-mythology-is-the-book-based">What kind of mythology is the book based on? Was trying to figure it out but wasn&#39;t sure.</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_454857'><a id="like_count_community_question_454857" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/454857?resource_type=CommunityQuestion"><span class="likesCount">2 likes</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F448873.The_Thief">like</a></span>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/12057984-sara"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1581260490i/12057984._UX100_CR0,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/12057984-sara">Sara</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">It's a mixture. I'm pretty sure the author herself said on a note that she wasn't trying to replicate any myths in particular, but instead got bits an<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">It's a mixture. I'm pretty sure the author herself said on a note that she wasn't trying to replicate any myths in particular, but instead got bits and pieces from different cultures that resulted in the mixture you find here. Some elements might seem familiar because of that.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=mythopoeic">mythopoeic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=newbery">newbery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=2017">2017</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer80282085" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12036171200514603116"><b>Update 12/29/2018</b><br/>Clearly I can never get tired of Megan Whalen Turner’s stories and Gen’s refreshing petulance.<br/><br/><b>Update 6/2011.</b> Let me just say, if you feel so-so about this book (like I did), please give its sequel - <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/40158.The_Queen_of_Attolia__The_Queen_s_Thief___2_' title='The Queen of Attolia (The Queen's Thief, #2) by Megan Whalen Turner' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Queen of Attolia</a> - a try. It made me forever and ever a dedicated fan of the series. <br/><br/><br/><br/>I have mixed feelings about this book. I enjoyed it, but I think I spoiled the experience for myself a little bit. <br/><br/><a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[The reviewers like to point to a huge twist at the end of the sto</span></span>
  <span id="freeText12036171200514603116" style="display:none"><b>Update 12/29/2018</b><br />Clearly I can never get tired of Megan Whalen Turner’s stories and Gen’s refreshing petulance.<br /><br /><b>Update 6/2011.</b> Let me just say, if you feel so-so about this book (like I did), please give its sequel - <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/40158.The_Queen_of_Attolia__The_Queen_s_Thief___2_" title="The Queen of Attolia (The Queen's Thief, #2) by Megan Whalen Turner" rel="nofollow noopener">The Queen of Attolia</a> - a try. It made me forever and ever a dedicated fan of the series. <br /><br /><br /><br />I have mixed feelings about this book. I enjoyed it, but I think I spoiled the experience for myself a little bit. <br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[The reviewers like to point to a huge twist at the end of the story as the biggest reason for enjoying this book. But if you know in advance that you should expect something, it is very easy to pick up clues on the way and figure out the big secret fairly quickly. I think this anticipation of the big reveal threw me off a bit and I ended up a little underwhelmed when the ending finally came. <br /><br />What I should have concentrated on is the writing, because it is superb. Turner shows a great command of English language, there is simply no word wasted in this story. Turner's books are highly recommended by Kristin Cashore, a great YA fantasy writer. In fact, the sentence structure, the tightness and simplicity of "The Thief" reminded me of "Graceling," only Turner is definitely a stronger writer. <br /><br />I also liked the thief himself. Gen is a funny, sneaky and extremely unreliable narrator, who holds a lot back and while he tells the story in his own words, he remains very anonymous throughout his adventures. I thought it was a very interesting way to write a book.<br /><br />Overall, I enjoyed this book, enough to want to read the consequent novels. However my advice would be - don't waste your time searching for clues and anticipating the huge climax and just enjoy the great writing and skillfully built fantasy world. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>
  <a data-text-id="12036171200514603116" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer153780421" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13325850606168945481"><a href='http://thebookgeek.co.uk' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379777457i/368079.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>My main reason for reading <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/448873.The_Thief__The_Queen_s_Thief___1_' title='The Thief (The Queen's Thief, #1) by Megan Whalen Turner' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Thief</a> was so I could read the sequel - <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/40158.The_Queen_of_Attolia__The_Queen_s_Thief___2_' title='The Queen of Attolia (The Queen's Thief, #2) by Megan Whalen Turner' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Queen of Attolia</a> - that I've heard is superb and far better than this first installment. I actually set myself up for quite an underwhelming experience with this book based on reviews and the fact that I'm not the biggest fan of more traditional fantasy with magical realms and such (I never could stand <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/33.The_Lord_of_the_Rings' title='The Lord of the Rings by J.R.R. Tolkien' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Lord of the Rings</a>). However, the story was interesting, the writing excellent and the protagonist was a witty, dev</span>
  <span id="freeText13325850606168945481" style="display:none"><a href="http://thebookgeek.co.uk" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379777457i/368079.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>My main reason for reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/448873.The_Thief__The_Queen_s_Thief___1_" title="The Thief (The Queen's Thief, #1) by Megan Whalen Turner" rel="nofollow noopener">The Thief</a> was so I could read the sequel - <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/40158.The_Queen_of_Attolia__The_Queen_s_Thief___2_" title="The Queen of Attolia (The Queen's Thief, #2) by Megan Whalen Turner" rel="nofollow noopener">The Queen of Attolia</a> - that I've heard is superb and far better than this first installment. I actually set myself up for quite an underwhelming experience with this book based on reviews and the fact that I'm not the biggest fan of more traditional fantasy with magical realms and such (I never could stand <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/33.The_Lord_of_the_Rings" title="The Lord of the Rings by J.R.R. Tolkien" rel="nofollow noopener">The Lord of the Rings</a>). However, the story was interesting, the writing excellent and the protagonist was a witty, devious little narrator that kept me entertained throughout.<br><br>I love the world that Turner has created, even though we've seen so little of it so far - this only served to further pique my interest. I see a lot of potential for this series and I have already ordered a copy of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/40158.The_Queen_of_Attolia__The_Queen_s_Thief___2_" title="The Queen of Attolia (The Queen's Thief, #2) by Megan Whalen Turner" rel="nofollow noopener">The Queen of Attolia</a>.<br><br>There is a twist that I thought was pretty obvious, and usually if I can solve a mystery it would suggest that it's about as mysterious as a gigantic billboard with flashing neon lights... but I think it had more to do with the fact that I knew a twist was coming, and some other GR reviewers were surprised by it. So, you know, try not to, um, think too much about it.<br><br>By the way, for people who have read this, isn't the biggest clue in <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[the title of the series? I noticed that early on and began to wonder... <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>But, for me, guessing the twist didn't spoil the story at all. I was introduced to a wonderful fantasy world, interesting characters, and a fast-paced plot, and it was all supported by Turner's talent for flawless writing. I cannot wait to read the second book.<br></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_1470110928" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1470110928" />
    <a title="Cristina Monica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica"><img alt="Cristina Monica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589617514p2/14596170.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1470110928?book_show_action=true">Dec 15, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cristina Monica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cristina Monica" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica">Cristina Monica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1470110928" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11018508134609173905"><br/><b>
  <i>Oh, thank gods, I thought. They’re going to leave me. All I want to do was lie in a dry prickly grass with my feet in a ditch forever. I could be a convenient sort of milemarker, I thought. Get to the thief and you know you are halfway to Methana. Wherever Methana might be.</i>
</b><br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/448873.The_Thief__The_Queen_s_Thief___1_' title='The Thief (The Queen's Thief, #1) by Megan Whalen Turner' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Thief</a> is a high fantasy with, like any other high fantasy on this planet, a journey the characters undertake. Gen, the main character was a pleasant surprise. While I first thought he was a feminine character, I was pr</span>
  <span id="freeText11018508134609173905" style="display:none"><br /><b>
  <i>Oh, thank gods, I thought. They’re going to leave me. All I want to do was lie in a dry prickly grass with my feet in a ditch forever. I could be a convenient sort of milemarker, I thought. Get to the thief and you know you are halfway to Methana. Wherever Methana might be.</i>
</b><br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/448873.The_Thief__The_Queen_s_Thief___1_" title="The Thief (The Queen's Thief, #1) by Megan Whalen Turner" rel="nofollow noopener">The Thief</a> is a high fantasy with, like any other high fantasy on this planet, a journey the characters undertake. Gen, the main character was a pleasant surprise. While I first thought he was a feminine character, I was proved wrong quite early in the story. Oops! That’s because many have compared this to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3236307.Graceling__Graceling_Realm___1_" title="Graceling (Graceling Realm, #1) by Kristin Cashore" rel="nofollow noopener">Graceling</a> and, as we know, that book’s lead character is a girl.<br /><br />But I loved male Gen. I was enchanted by his quick-witted personality and humour. He wasn’t boring or tedious but instead full of surprises and… skills! I liked how he never listened to anyone telling him how worthless he was and how he was someone who would open up to others who earned his trust. <br /><br />His looks were never widely described, which leaved place to some imagination digging, heh! As for the plot itself, it was long, slow and eventless. The only things that really saved it were the ending, which held many secrets and Gen himself… because he was that charming. Now I remember why I don’t read tons of high fantasy books. Oh well.<br /><br />I feel like the author wanted to create a special world building filled with history and linked to the background of the characters, but it failed miserably. It’s all about the GODS people believed or did not believe in… Who they were… How they became gods… But I wanted to know more about the people themselves, the places and the kings and queens. <br /><br />On a side and possibly spoiler-ish note…<br /><br />I’ll have to admit I was really disappointed when I discovered that Gen was not gay… because there were TONS of signs throughout the story! Clearly, I thought he would end up with Sophos. Every time Sophos blushed… Every time Gen touched him… THERE WAS A CONNECTION BETWEEN THOSE TWO. <br /><br />Grr.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11018508134609173905" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer8092010219695368247">a summary of this book in 20 words or less: <br/><br/>first half - an obscenely long journey where literally nothing happens.<br/>second half - item stolen and it all. kicks. off.<br/><br/><br/>as you can tell from my quick summary, the second half of this book is where its at. if you manage to get through the most boring horse ride in fictional history, then you will be well rewarded. you will get prison escapes, hot pursuits, clever planning, and not to mention more gen. i really liked gen. my goodness, he was charming. he</span>
  <span id="freeText8092010219695368247" style="display:none">a summary of this book in 20 words or less: <br /><br />first half - an obscenely long journey where literally nothing happens.<br />second half - item stolen and it all. kicks. off.<br /><br /><br />as you can tell from my quick summary, the second half of this book is where its at. if you manage to get through the most boring horse ride in fictional history, then you will be well rewarded. you will get prison escapes, hot pursuits, clever planning, and not to mention more gen. i really liked gen. my goodness, he was charming. he was honestly my main reason for pushing through the first half of the book - i just had to see how his role in the story played out.<br /><br />overall, this was a pretty decent read. it was short, but it has me interested enough to see how the rest of the series will go. even with the slow start of <i>‘the thief’</i>, i have a feeling the following books will be much better!<br /><br /><b>↠ <i>3.5 stars</i></b></span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/569393629" />
    <a title="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8734459-tadiana-night-owl"><img alt="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603085284p2/8734459.jpg" /></a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" href="/user/show/8734459-tadiana-night-owl">Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780140388343" href="/book/show/1082753.The_Thief">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=ya-fantasy">ya-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=i-own">i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer569393629" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13310595576958829698"><i>The Thief</i> is the first book in one of my favorite YA series EVER, with just a touch of Greek mythology-inspired fantasy to it. It can be just a little hard to get into at first, but the payoff at the end is brilliant, and the world-building is fantastic. Stick with it through at least the first three books and you won't regret it. <u>Avoid spoilers</u>.<br/><br/>Review originally posted at <a href='http://www.fantasyliterature.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Fantasy Literature</a>. <br/><br/>Megan Whalen Turner’s award-winning 1996 YA fantasy <i>The Thief</i>, set in a fantasy world that has very stro</span>
  <span id="freeText13310595576958829698" style="display:none"><i>The Thief</i> is the first book in one of my favorite YA series EVER, with just a touch of Greek mythology-inspired fantasy to it. It can be just a little hard to get into at first, but the payoff at the end is brilliant, and the world-building is fantastic. Stick with it through at least the first three books and you won't regret it. <u>Avoid spoilers</u>.<br><br>Review originally posted at <a href="http://www.fantasyliterature.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Fantasy Literature</a>. <br><br>Megan Whalen Turner’s award-winning 1996 YA fantasy <i>The Thief</i>, set in a fantasy world that has very strong echoes of ancient Greece, follows the adventures of Gen, the eponymous thief, as he is yanked from a filthy prison cell to go on a journey with a group of four men who hope to steal an unnamed object. The magus, who is leading the group, is the only person in the group who knows what they are searching for and where it is hidden.<br><br>In honor of the deep importance of mythology and the panoply of Greek-like gods in the tale of <i>The Thief</i>, several Greek gods and goddesses have graciously agreed to make guest appearances in this review, to add their brief thoughts and opinions regarding this book. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1436587671ra/15481112.gif" width="300" height="225" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><blockquote>
<b>ARTEMIS:</b> “Actually, when you think about it, the whole plot of <i>The Thief</i> revolves around a hunt. Okay, it’s a hunt for a hidden object, not a wild beast, but still. It’s really quite fascinating.”</blockquote>Gen spends most of the lengthy journey recovering from his months-long stay in prison, whining about their current conditions and the limited food, and sassing the magus and other members of the group. Although the journey is a rocky one, in more ways that just one, gradually Gen begins to gain respect for most of the group, and they for him.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1436587671i/15481113._SX540_.jpg" width="323" height="202" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><blockquote>
<b>POSEIDON:</b> “The role of the river Aracthus in protecting the treasure was a high point. But the story needed more bodies of water and less wasteland. Sea of Olives, pfft. Poor excuse for the real thing.”</blockquote>The characters are well-drawn and believable, with intriguing layers.<blockquote>… Ambiades was not going to move a step at the request of a worthless and insolent petty criminal. Ambiades, I realized, was the kind of person who liked to put people in a hierarchy, and he wanted me to understand that I was at the bottom of his. He was supposed to treat me politely in spite of my subservient position, and I was supposed to be grateful. For my part, I wanted Ambiades to understand that I considered myself a hierarchy of one.</blockquote>The tale of their journey is also interspersed with mythological tales of their world, such as the creation of the earth and birth of the gods, which give additional depth to the overall story.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1436587671i/15481114._SY540_.jpg" width="200" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><blockquote>
<b>ARES:</b> “I liked the sword fighting and the importance of the art of war in the plot of this story. Recognize! Too bad most of the fighting scenes were so short. But the conflicts between the countries of Sounis, Eddis and Attolia! Yeah, that has potential.”</blockquote>The first half of this book is somewhat slow-paced, as the group journeys to their destination, but once they arrive the pace quickens and the plot takes some unexpected and fascinating turns. <i>The Thief</i> has joined the list of my favorite YA fantasy novels.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1436587671i/15481115.jpg" width="250" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><blockquote>
<b>APHRODITE:</b> “Why does the most beautiful woman in the book only make a brief appearance? Where is the love?” *pouts*</blockquote>The Thief is the first book in a series of five books, with possibly more books to come, but can easily be enjoyed as a stand-alone novel. By the end of the book, I was a huge fan of the characters and of Megan Whalen Turner. I’ve bought all five books in this series and will probably automatically buy anything else she writes. THE QUEEN'S THIEF series shouldn't be missed by anyone who enjoys YA fantasy. In fact, my favorite book in the whole series is the third, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/40159.The_King_of_Attolia__The_Queen_s_Thief___3_" title="The King of Attolia (The Queen's Thief, #3) by Megan Whalen Turner" rel="nofollow noopener">The King of Attolia</a>.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1436587671i/15481116.jpg" width="183" height="298" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><blockquote>
<b>HERMES:</b> “I love how Eugenides, the god of thieves like *ahem* yours truly, is worshipped and honored by the main character. And did you notice how Eugenides doesn’t have to do any of the messengering crap? <i>How about that, there, Zeus?</i> Best book ever!”</blockquote>4½ stars, and a big "thank you" to my guest reviewers!</span>
  <a data-text-id="13310595576958829698" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2348973385" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2348973385" />
    <a title="Mary ~Ravager of Tomes~" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1452829-mary-ravager-of-tomes"><img alt="Mary ~Ravager of Tomes~" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598297811p2/1452829.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2348973385?book_show_action=true">Apr 03, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mary ~Ravager of Tomes~" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mary ~Ravager of Tomes~" href="/user/show/1452829-mary-ravager-of-tomes">Mary ~Ravager of Tomes~</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1452829-mary-ravager-of-tomes?shelf=year-2018">year-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1452829-mary-ravager-of-tomes?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1452829-mary-ravager-of-tomes?shelf=2-star">2-star</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2348973385" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4528079425865649378">Gen is a thief. The story begins with him being rescued from prison by the King's Magus in order to help him steal an object of political power that is so historically obscure it is almost considered a myth.<br/><br/><b>So there's a lot I didn't enjoy here.</b><br/><br/>To begin with, this book is mostly composed of a very, very, <i>very long</i> travelling sequence. Now, I should take this opportunity to point out that I don't dislike journey stories. In fact, one of my all time favorite novels is <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/33.The_Lord_of_the_Rings__The_Lord_of_the_Rings___1_3_' title='The Lord of the Rings (The Lord of the Rings, #1-3) by J.R.R. Tolkien' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Lord of the Rings</a>, which i</span>
  <span id="freeText4528079425865649378" style="display:none">Gen is a thief. The story begins with him being rescued from prison by the King's Magus in order to help him steal an object of political power that is so historically obscure it is almost considered a myth.<br><br><b>So there's a lot I didn't enjoy here.</b><br><br>To begin with, this book is mostly composed of a very, very, <i>very long</i> travelling sequence. Now, I should take this opportunity to point out that I don't dislike journey stories. In fact, one of my all time favorite novels is <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/33.The_Lord_of_the_Rings__The_Lord_of_the_Rings___1_3_" title="The Lord of the Rings (The Lord of the Rings, #1-3) by J.R.R. Tolkien" rel="nofollow noopener">The Lord of the Rings</a>, which is, at its core, a <b>massive journey.</b><br><br>The problem with this book is that <b>nothing even remotely interesting</b> happens while our characters are travelling. Somehow a relatively short 280 pages ends up feeling more like 2800 pages while trudging through scene after scene of riding on horses, campfire chatting, and bickering.<br><br>It was over halfway through the book before I really distinguished between all the side characters that weren't the Magus. And of course I had the unfortunate experience of accidentally imagining the Magus as Governor Ratcliffe, aka this guy:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1524439516ra/25418259.gif" width="470" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>So yea. That was.. not the book's fault but it was certainly interesting. <br><br>Anyway, once I finally had a firm handle on who everyone was, I realized they're mostly stereotypical in nature. Angry, masculine rival. Soft, young apprentice who isn't good with a sword. Tough, stoic guardian. <b>Eh.</b><br><br>I suppose it's important to remember that this was published in 1996, and so these stereotypes were probably a lot less abundant at that time. This definitely doesn't read like a modern Young Adult book, but this doesn't change the fact that my experience with these now is no more welcome than it would be reading a book published more recently. <br><br>The dynamic between the characters is even confusing for me. I have no idea how I'm supposed to feel about Gen or the Magus because their statements &amp; actions are just a <b>slew of contradictions.</b><br><br>One minute they're all messing around, joking, the next characters are threatening other characters with <b>actual, physical</b> violence. One minute Gen is at the complete mercy of the Magus, the next the Magus is allowing Gen to contradict his mythology stories without reprieve. <br><br><b>Gen even points out the Magus' inconsistency</b> so honestly, I'm just now sure how I'm supposed to view these characters.<br><br>Speaking of mythology, this book spends a lot of time exploring mythological characters of the realm &amp; telling their stories, and much less time than I would've liked expanding the world. These sections of the book come off very <u>info-dumpy,</u> and I could feel myself zoning out whenever they would pop up. <br><br>Honestly, I can only think of <i>one scene</i> where I chuckled near the beginning of this <b>boring trudge of a book.</b> Otherwise, I spent most of the time hoping it would be over soon.<br><br>Relieved to finally make it to the end of this story, I was planning to stick it with a 1 star &amp; forget about it. <b>But then something interesting happened.</b><br><br>The twist at the end practically flips this story on its head, contradicting everything you may have thought about it up to this point. <b>It's almost a brand new story</b> which is the <b>ONLY REASON</b> I am considering continuing the series. <br><br>I'm not 100% sure I agree with a twist like the one presented here. I'm not clear how it works, to be honest. It seems contradictory on many levels, but I'll definitely give it <b>points for originality.</b><br><br>This twist brought the book's rating up a bit for me. It doesn't make up for how hard the rest of the of it is to get through. 2 stars it will have to be, but I'm kind of excited to see where the story goes from here because it <b>feels like a fresh beginning.</b><br><br>Read this with the gorgeous miss <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen" rel="nofollow noopener">Kaylin!</a> ♥</span>
  <a data-text-id="4528079425865649378" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1237053624" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1237053624" />
    <a title="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31461418-alienor-french-frowner"><img alt="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1532688964p2/31461418.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1237053624?book_show_action=true">Mar 25, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" href="/user/show/31461418-alienor-french-frowner">Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=my-kindle-challenges-me">my-kindle-challenges-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=fave-characters">fave-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=2017-reads">2017-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1237053624" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15939857717315653909"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1501944489i/23512932._SX540_.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Huh. <b>I really, <i>really</i> liked this?</b> True enough, I've decided to start <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/448873.The_Thief__The_Queen_s_Thief___1_' title='The Thief (The Queen's Thief, #1) by Megan Whalen Turner' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Thief</a> in order to get to the sequels - that all my friends adore - and somehow I was at peace with the probable boredom I would feel during this first novel and... My enjoyment felt so <i>
  <b>effortless?</b>
</i> From the characters to the world and the writing, I've been enchanted. Truly. <br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>"I hate horses. I know people who think that they are noble, graceful animals, but regardless of what a horse looks like from a distance, never f</i></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText15939857717315653909" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1501944489i/23512932._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Huh. <b>I really, <i>really</i> liked this?</b> True enough, I've decided to start <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/448873.The_Thief__The_Queen_s_Thief___1_" title="The Thief (The Queen's Thief, #1) by Megan Whalen Turner" rel="nofollow noopener">The Thief</a> in order to get to the sequels - that all my friends adore - and somehow I was at peace with the probable boredom I would feel during this first novel and... My enjoyment felt so <i>
  <b>effortless?</b>
</i> From the characters to the world and the writing, I've been enchanted. Truly. <br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"I hate horses. I know people who think that they are noble, graceful animals, but regardless of what a horse looks like from a distance, never forget that it is as likely to step on your foot as look at you.<br>"What?" I dissembled.<br>"Get on the horse, you idiot."<br>"Me?"</i>
</blockquote><br>So there's <b>a lot of walking around</b> as I'm sure Fantasy writers are somewhat paid by hiking brands but eh! I wasn't bored. I said that! So. We're not confronted with Frodo and Sam level of walking, therefore I'm still here and not sleeping on my couch, drooling. That's something! And for those of you who swear by TLOTR, that's okay! We can be friends still! I'm not lending you my couch though. YOUR CHOICE. <br><br>Anyway, in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/448873.The_Thief__The_Queen_s_Thief___1_" title="The Thief (The Queen's Thief, #1) by Megan Whalen Turner" rel="nofollow noopener">The Thief</a>, Gen and his *cough* <i>companions</i> have a mission : to <b>steal a magical stone that will have the deplorable effect to give immense powers to the King of Sounis, a... complete asshole.</b> Don't be too hard on Gen, though : that's not as if the boy had a choice, being a prisoner and all. Their journey gives us the opportunity to learn more about the world <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/22542.Megan_Whalen_Turner" title="Megan Whalen Turner" rel="nofollow noopener">Megan Whalen Turner</a> created, as well as the characters and the complex relationship they develop between each other - there's more than meets the eyes, and I live for this stuff, okay?<br><br>And how I loved following these characters! <br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"For my part, I wanted Ambiades to understand that I considered myself a hierarchy of one."</i>
</blockquote><br>● Sophos, you're too sweet for this world, let me cuddle you what stop blushing <br>● Ambiades, what's your deal shut up shut up I am annoyed<br>● Magus, I've still not forgiven you for the beating <br>● Pol, ehhhhhhhhhhhhh<br>● <b>Gen! Little filthy mouth! Quick-witted and arrogant little thief! I ADORE YOU.</b> He shows just the right amount of selfishness and cleverness to appeal to me and I can't hide that I loved his voice. Indeed the story's told through his POV, and having started <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/40158.The_Queen_of_Attolia__The_Queen_s_Thief___2_" title="The Queen of Attolia (The Queen's Thief, #2) by Megan Whalen Turner" rel="nofollow noopener">The Queen of Attolia</a>, which is told in 3rd person POV, I can say this : The sequel's writing is objectively more elaborate and I really enjoy getting to know other characters and seeing Gen through other people eyes, <i>but</i> in my opinion <b>the choice of the first POV for this debut is perfect, needed, even, as it makes it so much easier to connect with Gen at first and I've never wanted to let go.</b> <i>Now</i> I'm ready to meet more characters, and the author's choice is perfect. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1501945431i/23513035._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Ohhhhh, and I know that some readers were annoyed by <b>the Mythology bits</b> but have you met me? Sure, the folklore is not so discreetly ripped straight from Greek Mythology, but as I LOVE these tales I was damn pleased. In the end, I am so, so curious about the directions <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/22542.Megan_Whalen_Turner" title="Megan Whalen Turner" rel="nofollow noopener">Megan Whalen Turner</a> will choose for her story, I cannot wait a day to find out. I need more. <br><br>Now, let me confess you something : <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/448873.The_Thief__The_Queen_s_Thief___1_" title="The Thief (The Queen's Thief, #1) by Megan Whalen Turner" rel="nofollow noopener">The Thief</a> tricked me... and I couldn't be more happy. If you're curious to know where my weird mind went, and you HAVE READ THE BOOK, please look at the spoiler below and... shake your head at me, I guess. I am shameless though, because being so far off made the experience even better.<br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Alright, so I know that 90% of my friends seem to have found out the truth about Gen, but I... didn't. I knew there was a twist, but to my delight, my hypothesis proved to be utterly wrong : I thought that maybe, Gen was a girl?? And I know, I KNOW, there are scenes where he strips down, but I could always convince myself that he could hide it, one way or another. Crazy, right? *awkward giggle* Even Sonos's reactions - when he acts so surprised that Gen's dad wanted him to be a soldier - fed my delusion XD <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>Oh, <i>well</i>. In the end, I am so glad I was wrong, and I can't recommend <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/448873.The_Thief__The_Queen_s_Thief___1_" title="The Thief (The Queen's Thief, #1) by Megan Whalen Turner" rel="nofollow noopener">The Thief</a> enough : even if this first novel is by no means astounding, <b>it's short, fun, and you'll meet the most endearing thief I've ever read about.</b> What more could a reader ask for, really? <br><br>PS. I'm sorry, this review is TERRIBLE, but I need to get to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/40158.The_Queen_of_Attolia__The_Queen_s_Thief___2_" title="The Queen of Attolia (The Queen's Thief, #2) by Megan Whalen Turner" rel="nofollow noopener">The Queen of Attolia</a> so... priorities, you know.<br><br><u>My reviews for the other books of the series</u> : <br>۩ Book 2, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2082723668?type=review#rating_127288808" rel="nofollow noopener">The Queen of Attolia</a> ★★★★ 1/2<br>۩ Book 3, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2083617029?type=review#rating_127283259" rel="nofollow noopener">The King of Attolia</a> ★★★★★ [ONE OF THE BEST BOOKS I'VE EVER READ]<br>۩ Book 4, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2084627754" rel="nofollow noopener">A Conspiracy of Kings</a> ★★★★<br><br><i>For more of my reviews, please visit:</i><br><blockquote>
  <a href="https://meetthebookworld.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1487851828i/22057164._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</blockquote></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_1995733992" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1995733992" />
    <a title="Elle (ellexamines)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/52545435-elle-ellexamines"><img alt="Elle (ellexamines)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582250895p2/52545435.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1995733992?book_show_action=true">Feb 01, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elle (ellexamines)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elle (ellexamines)" href="/user/show/52545435-elle-ellexamines">Elle (ellexamines)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780062642967" href="/book/show/30363359-the-thief">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=sff-high-fantasy">sff-high-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=y-notowned">y-notowned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=z-read2018">z-read2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=x-series">x-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=favorite-characters">favorite-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=z-coverporn">z-coverporn</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=3-star">3-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=y-out2000">y-out2000</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1995733992" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9144875185349298235">This felt like such a <b>classic</b> fantasy novel. You know those 2005-era books about journeys that you liked for some inexplicable reason? Yeah. That kind. <b>Except with really good worldbuilding and a lot of potential built up.</b><br/><br/>This novel follows Gen, a thief hired by a magus of Sunis to find a stone that gives the holder the right for rulership of Eddis. <br/>➽Sunis - the king’s county, attempting to take over Eddis<br/>➽Eddis - the country across, a country they must overtake<br/>➽Attolia - a country lying in betw</span>
  <span id="freeText9144875185349298235" style="display:none">This felt like such a <b>classic</b> fantasy novel. You know those 2005-era books about journeys that you liked for some inexplicable reason? Yeah. That kind. <b>Except with really good worldbuilding and a lot of potential built up.</b><br /><br />This novel follows Gen, a thief hired by a magus of Sunis to find a stone that gives the holder the right for rulership of Eddis. <br />➽Sunis - the king’s county, attempting to take over Eddis<br />➽Eddis - the country across, a country they must overtake<br />➽Attolia - a country lying in between, over which they must journey<br />➽Mead - a threatening country across the sea.<br />There’s clearly a lot of interesting potential set up in the worldbuilding realm, and I have a feeling things will get intense and political by the end. <br /><br />While the characters aren’t my favorite ever, a few have serious potential. Sophos is a really sweet character I wanted the best for. (Am I the only one who spent around eight pages thinking him and Gen would be a thing?) The magus is a character I started out hating and ended up sort of liking. Gen, our lead character, has a sarcastic sense of humor and a somewhat duplicitous narrative that made him easy to love. <br /><br />Something that stood out to me here was the subtle discussion around classism, the mage’s belief that Gen is lesser because he is an immigrant. Some of the things he said about Gen’s culture – the comments about how he knows Gen’s culture better than Gen’s mother did.<br /><br />My biggest thesis statement about this book - my most overreaching opinion, if you will - is that <b>this book is an extended prequel to what promises to be an intriguing series</b>. And not to offend anyone, but honestly: isn’t that every first book in every good series I’ve read in my life? I’ve heard a lot that the sequels to this get better, and I totally believe it — the worldbuilding here is so complex, so intricate, that a mediocre first book is almost needed to build it up. You can’t go straight to the climax - you have to go for the basic premise first. <br /><br />Hey, I’ve always said that <b>middle book syndrome is a myth and the middle book is usually better than book one in good series.</b> And I stand by that. So everyone agreeing with me for once is actually totally nice. <br /><br />Overall, while I didn’t think this was the most stunning book ever, <b>I’m super excited to continue on.</b> <br /><br /><b>
  <i>here are my other series thoughts:</i>
</b><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1995733992" rel="nofollow noopener">book one</a> - ★★★☆☆<br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2030955705" rel="nofollow noopener">book two</a> - ★★★★☆<br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2376881446" rel="nofollow noopener">book three</a> - ★★★★☆<br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2467555040" rel="nofollow noopener">book four</a> - ★★★★☆<br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2484905696" rel="nofollow noopener">book five</a> - ★★★★☆<br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2461451115" rel="nofollow noopener">book six</a> - TBD<br /><br /><a href="https://thebookishactress.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/52545435" rel="nofollow noopener">Goodreads</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/jespergayhey" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://www.youtube.com/channel/UCVIY_GxZIuclzsIw9CLSe3g" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a></span>

<div id="review_3539488197" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3539488197" />
    <a title="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell"><img alt="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1584062476p2/2190064.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3539488197?book_show_action=true">Sep 09, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" href="/user/show/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell">Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell?shelf=ya-ya-land">ya-ya-land</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell?shelf=kindle-clean-out-club">kindle-clean-out-club</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell?shelf=literary-sad-girl-canon">literary-sad-girl-canon</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3539488197" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2895487317177052602"><a href='https://readasaurus.blogspot.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1459070464i/18565492.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><a href='https://www.instagram.com/alwaysbeebooked/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Instagram</a> || <a href='https://twitter.com/NeniaCampbell' rel='nofollow noopener'>Twitter</a> || <a href='https://www.facebook.com/aficionenias/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Facebook</a> || <a href='http://www.amazon.com/Nenia-Campbell/e/B00AWVRKMS' rel='nofollow noopener'>Amazon</a> || <a href='https://www.pinterest.com/mightbeamisprin/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Pinterest</a><br/><br/><br/>I actually read this for the first time as a child back when it was still a standalone and I remember my edition had a really cheesy, cartoonish cover. THE THIEF is a book that won't appeal to everyone, and even as a child, I had difficulty getting into it. For one thing, <b>it's one of those fantasy novels that revolves around journeys</b>, which I know isn't everyone's cup of tea. For another, it's very slow-paced and mostly character-driven.</span>
  <span id="freeText2895487317177052602" style="display:none"><a href="https://readasaurus.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1459070464i/18565492.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a href="https://www.instagram.com/alwaysbeebooked/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> || <a href="https://twitter.com/NeniaCampbell" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> || <a href="https://www.facebook.com/aficionenias/" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> || <a href="http://www.amazon.com/Nenia-Campbell/e/B00AWVRKMS" rel="nofollow noopener">Amazon</a> || <a href="https://www.pinterest.com/mightbeamisprin/" rel="nofollow noopener">Pinterest</a><br><br><br>I actually read this for the first time as a child back when it was still a standalone and I remember my edition had a really cheesy, cartoonish cover. THE THIEF is a book that won't appeal to everyone, and even as a child, I had difficulty getting into it. For one thing, <b>it's one of those fantasy novels that revolves around journeys</b>, which I know isn't everyone's cup of tea. For another, it's very slow-paced and mostly character-driven. Towards the end, there's a series of rapid twists, but I think if you aren't into the characters or the world-building, it just isn't going to appeal, and that's fine. Not everybody loves everything.<br><br><br><br>THE THIEF is set in a pseudo-Ancient Grecian world, where three kingdoms-- Eddis, Sounis, and Attolia-- are constantly at odds, their ways changed and evolved over time following the influence of invaders. Attolia and Sounis are enemies, with Eddis to keep the peace and maintain trade, but of course, that doesn't always work.<br><br><br><br>Of course, Gen, our hero, doesn't know all that much about politics ostensibly, since he's a lowly thief currently biding his time in prison. He stole the king's seal and bragged about it in a bar, which resulted in his getting arrested and chained to his bed, denied even the creature comforts of exercise in the sun. When he's brought out for release by the king's magus, he's understandably suspicious: they want him for something and it isn't for cake decorating in celebration of his own release party. No, he's the "greatest" thief in the kingdom <b>and they want him to steal something BIG.</b><br><br><br><br>Reading this as an adult, I was struck by the maturity of this work. I'd often see it at Scholastic book fairs (remember those?) and I read it in grade school, I think. When I rate children's books and young adult low, I often get comments from people saying things like, "It's a kids' book, what did you expect?" which I think is a bit cheap, really, because it underestimates how clever kids are, and how layered a good YA or MG book should be. Children don't want to feel talked down to, and a really good book for preteens and teens should be as faceted as a diamond, because you want them to come back to it again and again and find new things every time they read it. Those are the books that become timeless.<br><br><br><br>With THE THIEF, <b>I picked up on a lot of clever banter and references that escaped me as a kid</b>. As a kid, I found Gen's sarcasm to the "adults" very funny and daring (even though I think Gen is an older teen/young man, he is a bit childish in a way that children will relate to). As an adult, he was still amusing but also quite exasperating-- but in a way that felt believable to his character. I was more interested in his developing relationships with the other people in his travel party (Ambiades, Sophos, Pol, and the magus), and how complex it became as we learned more about the other characters and their motivations. Turner also created her own mythology for this book, inspired by the Greek mythology, and that was really fun as well, to see how it paralleled the myths I'm familiar with.<br><br><br><br>While this isn't a book that will appeal to everyone, I think that anyone who enjoys fantasy books where the focus is on the development of the world and the characters, light political intrigue, and journeying will really enjoy this. At times, it almost has LORD OF THE RINGS vibes, and then at others, it feels more like <i>Indiana Jones</i>. This isn't a fast-paced, action-packed story until the end, but I really enjoyed it as a quiet sort of story that you can sink into until it springs on you. I look forward to reading the sequel.<br><br><br><br>4 stars</span>
  <a data-text-id="2895487317177052602" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2041161400?book_show_action=true">Feb 23, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Iryna *Book and Sword*" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Iryna *Book and Sword*" href="/user/show/57236678-iryna-book-and-sword">Iryna *Book and Sword*</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2041161400" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3860669925787346694"><b>1.5/5 stars</b> <br/>Good riddance!!! <br/><br/>I must have read a different book than everybody else had because I cannot for the life of me comprehend how this book has won any literal awards. <br/><br/>As an avid fantasy reader I can tell you that this book is as close to a "riveting fantasy novel" as flour is to being a spice.<br/>Why flour you ask?<br/>Beuase it reminds me of this book - dry, bland and boring. <br/><br/>​And I really tried to tie this book all of the chances I could. I wanted to dnf it after 30 pages, but:<br/>1. I was told th</span>
  <span id="freeText3860669925787346694" style="display:none"><b>1.5/5 stars</b> <br />Good riddance!!! <br /><br />I must have read a different book than everybody else had because I cannot for the life of me comprehend how this book has won any literal awards. <br /><br />As an avid fantasy reader I can tell you that this book is as close to a "riveting fantasy novel" as flour is to being a spice.<br />Why flour you ask?<br />Beuase it reminds me of this book - dry, bland and boring. <br /><br />​And I really tried to tie this book all of the chances I could. I wanted to dnf it after 30 pages, but:<br />1. I was told that it gets much better as the book goes on. <b>It didn't.</b><br />2. I was told that series get much, much better. I still have to see that for myself. One day.<br />3. I scored 4 books from this series at a thrift store for dirt cheap in mint condition, so I wanted to give it a chance before I donate all of them back and forget I ever wasted my time on them. <br /><br />But Iryna, what about that awesome twist at the end? <br />I'm sorry, but that twist? I guessed "the twist" pretty early in the beginning of the book. I'm not saying that I'm Sherlock Holmes (okay sometimes I pretend I am), but after reading many fantasy books that twist is not so twisty anymore - pretty standard trick, if you ask me. <br /><br />​I can sum up about 85 percent of this book in few sentences.<br />​Gen (main character) whines, Gen is tired, Gen is hungry, Gen is being a smart mouth, Gen is hungry, Gen is tired, Gen is hungry. The words <i>"I'm hungry" and "so I took a nap"</i> were probably said at least 20 times. If you are looking for the world's most annoying fiction character, you may stop now. Gen got the prize (in my eyes at least). The rest 15 percent were taken up with all the action that this book decided to throw at us and some political intrigues. By that point I just wanted it all to be just over so I could move on with my reading life. <br />​<br />The book is a 280 pages, and it took me 9 days to read it. 9 days! Why? Because I was so unbelievably, out of my mind, ripping my hair out - bored. <br />Was the twist at the end worth the 200 pages of redundancy and absolutely nothing happening? No, no it was not. <br /><br />I know I sound very bitter right now, but I was genuinely excited for this book. And it let me down, big time. I hated the first person narrative, and I loathed Gen as a narrator even more. Side characters were bland, world building was okay at best and the plot didn't go anywhere till the last 30 pages. <br /><br />​Despite all of this I will (not soon, but sometime) continue with the book 2. I didn't suffer through this for nothing, I will see for myself if the series do indeed get better. My hopes are very low though. Lower than low. <br />Also I looked ahead and book 2 is written in third person, which is an improvement because I don't like first person narration fantasy, BUT who writes first book in first person and then switches to the third person? Who does that? Why?<br /><br />My <a href="http://bookandsword.net " rel="nofollow noopener">WEBSITE</a><br />My <a href="https://www.instagram.com/book_and_sword/" rel="nofollow noopener">INSTAGRAM</a><br />My <a href="https://bookandswordblog.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">WORDPRESS BLOG</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="3860669925787346694" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_37116717" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/37116717" />
    <a title="Keith" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1290678-keith"><img alt="Keith" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1214963010p2/1290678.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/37116717?book_show_action=true">Nov 07, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Keith" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Keith" href="/user/show/1290678-keith">Keith</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780688146276" href="/book/show/1082754.The_Thief">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer37116717" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17301882081378330680">This was another book my wife insisted that I read. It was our before-bed read aloud book last month.<br/><br/>Reading 10-15 pages a night, the first half of the book was enjoyable, but unfolded rather slowly. I was a bit puzzled about why my wife was so enthusiastic about the book. Then, about half way through, the excitement and tempo increased a few notches, and it become a real page-turner.<br/><br/>This is a fantasy novel, but it is not your typical swords and sorcery adventure. There are swords, and even a co</span>
  <span id="freeText17301882081378330680" style="display:none">This was another book my wife insisted that I read. It was our before-bed read aloud book last month.<br /><br />Reading 10-15 pages a night, the first half of the book was enjoyable, but unfolded rather slowly. I was a bit puzzled about why my wife was so enthusiastic about the book. Then, about half way through, the excitement and tempo increased a few notches, and it become a real page-turner.<br /><br />This is a fantasy novel, but it is not your typical swords and sorcery adventure. There are swords, and even a couple of fights, but the closest we get to sorcery are some mysterious occurrences that could best be described as super-natural. Turner's alternate reality evokes the feeling of Greece. The landscape is rocky, somewhat mountainous, and filled with olive trees. The "old" religion has the feeling of Greek mythology although the divinities are mostly different. And the political backdrop is a set of small rivalrous kingdoms that could be stand-ins for the city-states of ancient Greece. <br /><br />The story is told (first person) by Gen, a thief who opens the book imprisoned in the kingdom of Sounis. He is freed by the King's Magus---a wiseman-type councilor---who needs a skilled thief to help him recover a lost artifact. They set out on this expedition, accompanied by the Magus's two apprentices and a soldier. In the first half of the book, we slowly get to know the characters through Gen's eyes, and learn something of the world where this story is set. Turner does a good job developing and describing the mix of relationships between the members of this quest---rivalries, respect, jealousy---and as we get to know the characters better, it becomes apparent that there is a bit more to each of them than meets the eye. <br /><br />Midway through the book, just when it seems that the entire plot is going to be character-driven, the tempo increases dramatically. There are fights, escapes, chases. Amongst this action there are still the puzzles of characters whose motivations we don't entirely understand---including our narrator, who carefully hides a few secrets of his own until the end. <br /><br />All-in-all, a well-told story, with a good combination of plot, characters, and an interesting setting.<br /><br />Once again, my wife picked a winner. I should pay more attention to her recommendations.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17301882081378330680" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_670977579" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/670977579" />
    <a title="Lois Bujold" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7672661-lois-bujold"><img alt="Lois Bujold" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442449462p2/7672661.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/670977579?book_show_action=true">Jul 18, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lois Bujold" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lois Bujold" href="/user/show/7672661-lois-bujold">Lois Bujold</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">everyone</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Lois by: </span>
      e-mail correspondent years ago who loved it so much she mailed me a copy
  </div>


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer670977579" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12728297932038004674">Having dutifully tried a few new things to my lack of satisfaction this past week, I turned instead to an old favorite that I knew would be a pleasurable read. This is a book that re-repays a re-re-read, not only soon, but after finishing its sequels once they widen one's view of its world and characters.<br/><br/>There is not too much one can say about <i>The Thief</i> that is not a spoiler, and this is a book that should NOT be read with preconceptions. Set in an alternate fantasy world loosely inspired by Gre</span>
  <span id="freeText12728297932038004674" style="display:none">Having dutifully tried a few new things to my lack of satisfaction this past week, I turned instead to an old favorite that I knew would be a pleasurable read. This is a book that re-repays a re-re-read, not only soon, but after finishing its sequels once they widen one's view of its world and characters.<br /><br />There is not too much one can say about <i>The Thief</i> that is not a spoiler, and this is a book that should NOT be read with preconceptions. Set in an alternate fantasy world loosely inspired by Greece both ancient and medieval, it opens with a bedraggled young thief, Gen, being plucked from the king's prison in Sounis to accompany the king's magus on a peculiar quest, for which his talents will be needed. Written as a first person memoir in Gen's engaging voice, it is classified as YA, and was a Newbery Honor book when it first came out in 1996, but really, I mention this mainly to make the book easier to find in a library or bookstore. Simply written but never simple.<br /><br />Trust me. Just read it. Then read it again, because it will not be the same river twice.<br /><br />It has at this time three follow-ups, <i>The Queen of Attolia</i>, <i>The King of Attolia</i>, and <i>A Conspiracy of Kings</i>, of which my favorite is <i>The King of Attolia</i>. These should be read in strict order for the best and most delightful effect and to avoid big honking spoilers.<br /><br />I do wonder, idly, if Turner has been unduly constrained in further development of the series by the book's YA-market origins. It seems to me further expansion would require shifting to adult-market fantasy as the main characters age out of YA parameters, which would be tricky but not impossible to bring off. If it were to be kept YA it would almost have to jump to the next generation, which also has possibilities, but may not be where it (or its writer) wants to go. <br /><br />Ta, L.<br /> </span>
  <a data-text-id="12728297932038004674" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer56833127" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18344408979188585216">What do you do when you want to gain possession of something that's nearly impossible to obtain? You hire a thief who can steal just about anything.<br/><br/>Gen has no disillusions about his abilities as a thief. He's actually named after the god of thieves, Eugenides, as a matter of fact. While his father wanted him to be a soldier, he knew that was not the life for him. Instead, he honed his skills at stealing, until he was one of the best in the land. Too bad he did a little too much bragging about st</span>
  <span id="freeText18344408979188585216" style="display:none">What do you do when you want to gain possession of something that's nearly impossible to obtain? You hire a thief who can steal just about anything.<br /><br />Gen has no disillusions about his abilities as a thief. He's actually named after the god of thieves, Eugenides, as a matter of fact. While his father wanted him to be a soldier, he knew that was not the life for him. Instead, he honed his skills at stealing, until he was one of the best in the land. Too bad he did a little too much bragging about stealing the King's seal and ended up in jail. He's approached by the King's magus and offered a proposition, steal something for the King, and he'll be released from jail. If he refuses, he'll simply disappear (not in a good way). It's not a proposition an intelligent young man would say no to. So begins this story.<br /><br />Gen is one of those characters that I couldn't help but enjoy. His irreverent, jaundiced, but very insightful view of human nature insinuated him into my affections. I like that kind of humor, so I tend to gravitate towards main characters like Gen. From the beginning, I knew he was a thief, but that didn't make him unlikeable to me. Instead, I wanted to find out what made him tick, and I was rooting for him to come out of this story for the better. I liked that I saw some character growth in him as this story progressed.<br /><br />The Thief is a story set in an alternate world in which various gods hold the devotion of the populace. I liked how part of the story was hearing the tales of the gods who made this world; and those stories are very smoothly integrated into the plot, playing a crucial role in the narration, characterization, and the unfolding of this story. Reading the extra material at the end of this novel revealed Ms. Turner's thought process. I could see a heavy Greek mythology influence, but there were unique elements about the pantheon and the story-telling that showed the author's specific vision. There are also aspects that surprised me, in that the gods actually play a real role in this story. I liked how the fantasy elements didn't dominate, but the focus is Gen's character and his quest to steal something that has the potential to affect three kingdoms in this novel.<br /><br />There was an interesting twist towards the end that I was not expecting at all, and I always give my respect to an author who can do that, and surprise me. I'm not a jaded reader, by any means, but I read a lot, and I've seen a lot of common plot devices; so a writer who can throw me a curve ball is always appreciated.<br /><br />I have to say that this Newbury Award Winner did impress me. It's one of those stories that doesn't try to go elaborate, but has a richness that won me over as a reader all the same. Fortunately, this is part of a series, so I can look forward to more adventures in this interesting world. </span>
  <a data-text-id="18344408979188585216" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer18016273363549571933">I can't say this book is bad but it isn't great either. Boring interactions and dull protagonist with the plot I couldn't care less about. Nothing even slightly exciting happens. The start reminds me a bit of "Throne of Glass" series and that's the only good thing about this book.   <span id="freeText18016273363549571933" style="display:none">I can't say this book is bad but it isn't great either. Boring interactions and dull protagonist with the plot I couldn't care less about. Nothing even slightly exciting happens. The start reminds me a bit of "Throne of Glass" series and that's the only good thing about this book. I'm not even a big fan of Throne of Glass.<br /><br />A thief named Gen got out from jail in order to help a Magus steal an ancient treasure. When the identity of the thief is finally revealed I was occasionally interested in the plot, but not enough to care. Gen had been locked up because he bragged too much about stealing the King’s seal. Gen has his own agenda. All that mythology was bland as hell too. <br /><br />I got through the first 100 pages with hope it'll get better, because I was told it would. The writing style was too factographic and lifeless. I wasn't interested in the world setting and didn't like any of the characters. I won't be coming back for the sequel, definitely. I couldn't connect to the characters and the whole time I was waiting for something to happen, but nothing essentially did. Suddenly I was at the end with poor excuse for a plot twist. This book has a very slow pace with almost non-existent plot. They've started their journey, and then traveled, and traveled, and traveled. And yes, you guessed it - they traveled. Maybe I should've found the banter interesting, but I didn't. I started skipping it at some point. <br /><br />Gen is obnoxious, underdeveloped, uninteresting and annoying. He's like a male version of Celaena Sardothien. His brilliancy didn't do much for me. He's so arrogant in playing his role that I really lost interest in whether he'll succeed or not. He tried so hard to be sassy and witty, but none of it had any impact on me.</span>
