        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1127617227" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18299740870953601902">Buddy read with some friends at <b>
  <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/148164-buddies-books-and-baubles' rel='nofollow noopener'>Buddies Books and Baubles</a>
</b><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>I am a master of foolhardy plans, I thought. I have so much practice I consider them professional risks.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br/>EVERYONE told me not to expect much from this book and to be patient. They said the beginning isn’t very good but the second half is pretty good and the next two books are amazing…so just hang in there. Well I found that to be true and false at the same time.<br/><br/>It is true the second half of this book is much more interesting</span>
  <span id="freeText18299740870953601902" style="display:none">Buddy read with some friends at <b>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/148164-buddies-books-and-baubles" rel="nofollow noopener">Buddies Books and Baubles</a>
</b><br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>I am a master of foolhardy plans, I thought. I have so much practice I consider them professional risks.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br />EVERYONE told me not to expect much from this book and to be patient. They said the beginning isn’t very good but the second half is pretty good and the next two books are amazing…so just hang in there. Well I found that to be true and false at the same time.<br /><br />It is true the second half of this book is much more interesting, there is more going on action wise and the last 100 pages just fly by. But the first half isn’t that shabby either if you are paying attention. The only reason parts of it felt a little long are the backstories to the gods feathered in a little like info-dumping. They are interesting lore stories but it is unclear how they fit into the book until later and almost felt like filler while I was reading them. However with Gen the Master Thief there are clues to be found and double meanings to a few things that don’t become clear until the end of the book. I found it to be quite entertaining trying to figure out who/what Gen really is and what his true purpose was.<br /><br /> But even if you find the first half a little dull this is a short book at only about 215 pages so it really doesn’t take that long to go through and figuring out Gen’s story is totally worth it. He is a lot of fun to read as he is antagonizing his traveling companions.<br /><blockquote>
  <i>While we ate, I picked at the magus. I liked to watch him lose his temper and then regain it when he remembered that I was supposed to be beneath his contempt.</i>
</blockquote><br />I did guess quite a few things about Gen correctly, but I also guessed just as many wrong so there were still some surprises to be had and enough interest generated about the three kingdoms in the story that I’d be interested in continuing.<br /><br />Even though this book is listed as MG/YA it didn’t really read that way and I hear the later books are more adult than this one. Overall a really quick fun read that had action, mystery, betrayal and a few unexpected surprises that made it all the more interesting to read.<br /></span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/17683108?book_show_action=true">Mar 13, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer17683108" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9143437983553979131">A thief sprung from jail to help a Magnus steal an ancient treasure, warring kingdoms, political intrigue, sword fights, narrow escapes,a mythology invented especially for this fictional place, and a quest--everything, it would seem, to keep me reading. So I am wondering why I so disliked this book that I had to force myself to keep reading to the end. I think I hit upon the answer spoken by one of Turner's characters near the last weary lap of the book: "Oh, fine," I told him...but I didn't rea</span>
  <span id="freeText9143437983553979131" style="display:none">A thief sprung from jail to help a Magnus steal an ancient treasure, warring kingdoms, political intrigue, sword fights, narrow escapes,a mythology invented especially for this fictional place, and a quest--everything, it would seem, to keep me reading. So I am wondering why I so disliked this book that I had to force myself to keep reading to the end. I think I hit upon the answer spoken by one of Turner's characters near the last weary lap of the book: "Oh, fine," I told him...but I didn't really care. I didn't care much about anything..." And that is my experience with this book in a nutshell. The characters never matter to me. Gen, the thief, is so arrogant and obnoxious in playing his role that I could really care less about whether he succeeds. And the other characters are never really fleshed out enough for them to matter to me either. By the end of the book when the identity of the thief is finally revealed I began to have moments of interest, but not enough to be anxious to read the sequels.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9143437983553979131" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2240060368" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2240060368" />
    <a title="✨    jamieson   ✨" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7706640-jamieson"><img alt="✨    jamieson   ✨" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1499961431p2/7706640.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2240060368?book_show_action=true">Jan 02, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="✨    jamieson   ✨" class="user" itemprop="url" name="✨    jamieson   ✨" href="/user/show/7706640-jamieson">✨    jamieson   ✨</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=series-to-complete">series-to-complete</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=2018-reads">2018-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2240060368" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6403951587353921680"><b>this is one of those books where I liked it, and then I didn't like it, and then I was gonna dnf it, and then I liked it again, and then I was bored again, and then all of a sudden I loved it</b> Essentially, a really big rollercoaster of emotions. Overall coming out of this I do feel it was a positive experience hence a three star rather than two, but there was some close calls. <br/><br/>I started this because I LOVE thief stories. I will continue to keep reading stories about thieves and heists until the d</span>
  <span id="freeText6403951587353921680" style="display:none"><b>this is one of those books where I liked it, and then I didn't like it, and then I was gonna dnf it, and then I liked it again, and then I was bored again, and then all of a sudden I loved it</b> Essentially, a really big rollercoaster of emotions. Overall coming out of this I do feel it was a positive experience hence a three star rather than two, but there was some close calls. <br /><br />I started this because I LOVE thief stories. I will continue to keep reading stories about thieves and heists until the day of my death because <u>I LOVE THEM</u>. On the surface this is a pretty basic thief story - We follow Gen, a notorious thief taken out of jail and charged by the king of Sunis to find an ancient stone. Whoever possesses the stone gains rightful leadership of the country called Eddis. <br /><br /><b>So the beginning part of this book is really boring</b>. The first half follows Gen, the Magus who pulls him from prison and three soldiers as they travel to the fabled location of the stone. Literally nothing happens in this section and I considered dnf'ing the book. &lt;<br /><br />b&gt;There isn't much to cling to at the start the writing is a little stale and uninspiring. The characters didn't really .. do anything. Often their actions and behaviours contradicted earlier behaviour and it was hard to get an understanding of their personalities. The three soliders were all very one dimensional to me and hard to tell apart. <u>One thing I DID appreciate was the unreliable narrator</u> I love unreliable narrators and it was used really well in the second section. <br /><br />This book definitely picks up in the second half. There is significantly more action and the politics and worldbuilding introduced through section one starts to come into play. In this section, Megan Whaler Turner turns your expectations on their head and if you liked the ending of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/19161852.The_Fifth_Season__The_Broken_Earth___1_" title="The Fifth Season (The Broken Earth, #1) by N.K. Jemisin" rel="nofollow noopener">The Fifth Season</a> I think you'd like this book too (it's not the same thing, but it's got a similar <i>vibe</i>)<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>And the Earth had no name. The gods know themselves and have no need of names. It is man who names all things, even gods.</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />Definitely the highlight of this book was the politics introduced and how this is going to play out in the next books. I liked the discussions around class, social structure and war here. There is a lot of discussion about culture and immigration, and the perception that lower class, uneducated people are inherently less valuable than upper class educated people. The thematic work is, I think, the greatest strength of this book. And Turner has tied it into the general politics and worldbuilding in such a way I know it's going to keep coming up, and I'm really happy about that. <br /><br /><b>This reads like a giant prologue but I think it's going in a great direction</b>. Even though I truly disliked the first bit I truly enjoyed the final part. I would love to see the characters get fleshed out some more, but if that happened, and the political intrigue keeps on this trajectory, I think this could be a series I really enjoy. <br /><br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6403951587353921680" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_78419089" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/78419089" />
    <a title="Lara" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/309689-lara"><img alt="Lara" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1465346130p2/309689.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/78419089?book_show_action=true">Nov 20, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lara" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lara" href="/user/show/309689-lara">Lara</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780140388343" href="/book/show/1082753.The_Thief">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/309689-lara?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/309689-lara?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/309689-lara?shelf=abandoned">abandoned</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer78419089" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15208960488564787115">I'm giving up on this one. It's not BAD, just...excruciatingly BORING. To me, anyway. I found the main character obnoxious and all the other characters underdeveloped and uninteresting, and over half way through the book, nothing's really happened--they've started their journey, and then traveled, and traveled, and traveled, and traveled, and traveled, and...you get the picture. I've heard really good things about this series, and maybe at some point in the future I'll give it another try. But I</span>
  <span id="freeText15208960488564787115" style="display:none">I'm giving up on this one. It's not BAD, just...excruciatingly BORING. To me, anyway. I found the main character obnoxious and all the other characters underdeveloped and uninteresting, and over half way through the book, nothing's really happened--they've started their journey, and then traveled, and traveled, and traveled, and traveled, and traveled, and...you get the picture. I've heard really good things about this series, and maybe at some point in the future I'll give it another try. But I have too many other books that look far more exciting than this one has been, so I'm moving on to one of them.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15208960488564787115" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2080370443" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2080370443" />
    <a title="Sunny ✨wordslikefury✨" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32222897-sunny-wordslikefury"><img alt="Sunny ✨wordslikefury✨" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1574318791p2/32222897.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2080370443?book_show_action=true">Feb 11, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sunny ✨wordslikefury✨" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sunny ✨wordslikefury✨" href="/user/show/32222897-sunny-wordslikefury">Sunny ✨wordslikefury✨</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780062642967" href="/book/show/30363359-the-thief">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32222897-sunny-wordslikefury?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32222897-sunny-wordslikefury?shelf=ya-fantasy">ya-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32222897-sunny-wordslikefury?shelf=2018-reads">2018-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32222897-sunny-wordslikefury?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32222897-sunny-wordslikefury?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2080370443" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14755380044440890586">The Thief deserves more stars than I am giving it. It’s a <b>wonderful and captivating</b> story about a thief who is freed from prison to steal something only heard of in a fairy tale for the king. This task is basically the road to his freedom. So what choice does he have but to take the offer? It’s either this…or spend his days in prison in suffering and torture.<br/><br/>Our protagonist, Gen, is so full of wits. I found his personalty to be the best part of the story. From his sarcastic comments to his brood</span>
  <span id="freeText14755380044440890586" style="display:none">The Thief deserves more stars than I am giving it. It’s a <b>wonderful and captivating</b> story about a thief who is freed from prison to steal something only heard of in a fairy tale for the king. This task is basically the road to his freedom. So what choice does he have but to take the offer? It’s either this…or spend his days in prison in suffering and torture.<br /><br />Our protagonist, Gen, is so full of wits. I found his personalty to be the best part of the story. From his sarcastic comments to his broody manner, everything about him was entertaining. So why exactly did I not give it a higher rating? Well…<b>I found the writing to be too descriptive.</b> Yes…there is such a thing. I love when books are through in telling a story, but there is a thing as too much.<br /><br />I didn’t want to know every single detail. I didn’t need to know the exact feet of distance from that block of wood to that piece of stone. I didn’t need to know exactly how parallel one object was from another. I barely had room to use my imagination because EVERYTHING was laid out for me. Turner’s writing is easy to understand, but I think <b>the book could have worked with less descriptiveness.</b> This doesn’t mean Turner’s words are boring. Her writing displays an epic journey to success, showcasing character development as well as plot twists and light suspense. I was on par with predicting the plot twist. I think anyone can figure it out if you really pay attention. <br /><br />This book is perfect for fantasy lovers. I will say however, this book sides with more <b>classic and traditional fantasy.</b> It is very slow paced, especially the first half, but this is the kind of series where <b>the first book is just setting up for the second one,</b> which I heard is far more superior in terms of story telling, writing, and character development.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14755380044440890586" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_64036708" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/64036708" />
    <a title="TheBookSmugglers" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1223249-thebooksmugglers"><img alt="TheBookSmugglers" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1316717753p2/1223249.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/64036708?book_show_action=true">Jul 18, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="TheBookSmugglers" class="user" itemprop="url" name="TheBookSmugglers" href="/user/show/1223249-thebooksmugglers">TheBookSmugglers</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer64036708" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18394080246783688358"><a href='http://thebooksmugglers.com/2009/07/i-love-this-series-the-queens-thief-by-megan-whalen-turner.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>Full Review Link</a><br/><br/>It is safe to say that I spend most of my free time reading. I read three to four books every week, sometimes more. I am very careful with what I choose to read which means that most of the books I read, I end up enjoying at least to some degree. But it is rare, extremely rare, to read a book that falls in that category of Books for Life. You know the ones: those that take over your heart and your mind, that even when you are reading you know that you are experiencing something u</span>
  <span id="freeText18394080246783688358" style="display:none"><a href="http://thebooksmugglers.com/2009/07/i-love-this-series-the-queens-thief-by-megan-whalen-turner.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Full Review Link</a><br /><br />It is safe to say that I spend most of my free time reading. I read three to four books every week, sometimes more. I am very careful with what I choose to read which means that most of the books I read, I end up enjoying at least to some degree. But it is rare, extremely rare, to read a book that falls in that category of Books for Life. You know the ones: those that take over your heart and your mind, that even when you are reading you know that you are experiencing something unique, a connection with a story and its characters (that only serial readers can understand); those that you know will remain with you, forever.<br /><br />I experienced such rapture when I read The Name of the Wind by Patrick Rothfuss earlier in the year, and to my utter surprise and delight, again a few weeks ago when I finally read The Queen’s Thief series by Megan Whalen Turner.<br /><br />This series came under my radar only recently when Angie from Angieville started to blog about the books with not a little amount of excitement. From then on, I started to see more and more people talking about them with such fervor that I thought I should give them a try. And, HOLY GUACAMOLE.<br /><br />I am totally, irrevocably, head over heels in love with this series. I knew I would have to review these books eventually, I had hoped to do so during this YA Month but I also realised that I had a decision to make: I could either review each book in the series separately or I could review the series as whole. The former would naturally lead to spoilers being revealed and since these books cannot, should not be spoiled, I opted for the latter by writing an overall review of the series, spoiler free. This is what I am trying to do here – although I am fully aware that so far, I only managed to basically behave like a fan-girl.<br /><br />But it cannot be helped. I now completely understand the fervor, the excitement that this series inspire. As I was reading the books, as the pages were being turned I had only one thought in mind: this is why I read. THIS is why I read. THIS IS WHY I READ. And it all comes down to one word: Eugenides.<br /><br />Gen, Eugenides is a thief. He boasts that he can steal anything. That lands him in the King of Sounis’ prison where he spends a couple of months until he is offered, by the King’s Magus, his freedom but in return he has to steal something that people don’t even think really exists.<br /><br /><br /><br />This is how the whole thing opens, in The Thief and we are told about this expedition in search of the Gift, by Gen himself, a humorous narrator of this dashing adventure across the neighbouring countries of Sounis, Eddis and Attolia. This person, this ragamuffin, lazy, starved boy – can he really steal anything?<br /><br />But you see, Gen is extremely clever, a fact which the reader and his companions in the first adventure, come to slowly realise. Close to the end of that book, we learn something that is crucial to the entire series – that Gen is actually cleverer than anyone else. And there is something else too, something that makes him important. But that doesn’t matter to us here and now, because what really matters is how amazing Gen is. By the end of book 1, it is impossible not to like the guy or his “voice”.<br /><br /><br /><br />Then book 2 starts, and shock of the shocks. Gen is no longer the narrator – the narrative has shifted to third person with Gen’s, the Queen of Eddis’ and the Queen of Attolia’s PoV. At first, it is almost painful to lose Gen’s narration but then somewhere in the middle of the reading it hits you with a certainty:<br /><br />OF COURSE the narrative has to change.<br /><br />Because this is a different book. It is still the same story but progress has been made. Because now, the destiny of countries is at stake, war is brewing in the horizon between Attolia, Eddis and Sounis. This is a more sophisticated book, it has political discussion , political intrigue, it discusses the role that the Gods play in the fate of men and nations.<br /><br />In the beginning of the series, Gen is a boy. A cocky, impetuous, adventurous, conniving boy. When book 2 starts, something terrible happens (did I say shock of the shocks before? Well, this is even more shocking) that shapes the man Eugenides becomes. A man who has now to steal more than a simple object: he is tasked to steal a man, a woman and peace.<br /><br />The way he does it, takes us back to more twists like in the first book. And we, once again, are surprised by how clever Eugenides is. Even if we expect it by now.<br /><br /><br /><br />Then book 3 starts. Once again, a shock. The book is entirely from the point of view of a character we never saw before. As the book progresses, the certainty hits once more:<br /><br />OF COURSE the narrative has to change.<br /><br />Because this time, this time we KNOW how clever Gen is. But no one else does. Including Costis, the narrator, a member of the Queen of Attolia’s Guard who commits the mistake of underestimating Eugenides. And this is the genius of Megan Whalen Turner because in book 3, we, the readers, are Eugenides’s accomplices. We sit back and wait for the coin to drop for everybody else as it has dropped for us in books 1 and 2. This is about pay-off, about Eugenides stealing respect and a kingdom. And what a story this is.<br /><br />This is a series of books that have deep meanings, hidden clues throughout the story. Where everything matters from the type of clothes someone wears, to the reason behind a pair of earrings being worn at a particular right time, to the declaration of love that the raising of one’s eyebrow is.<br /><br />And speaking of love: there is also romance in these books. It starts towards the middle of book 2 and it takes centre stage in book 3. But not in it a blatant way: the romance is subtle, almost private (especially in book 3) and I am not exaggerating when I say it is the most amazing romance I have read of late. It is unexpected and it is unusual. For starters, Eugenides is shorter and younger than the person he loves. But she is everything he ever wanted and he is everything she ever needed. Because of that, their dynamic is simply awesome and there is no other word for it. And what Eugenides is to his lady is aw-worthy at the same time that it is powerful. This is good stuff, plain and simple.<br /><br />To sum up: I was lost in the world of Attolia and Eddis and I did not want to get away from it. I would be remiss if I didn’t say one last thing: that the female characters in the series are extremely capable, intelligent, strong, and I admired both of then, the two Queens, as different as they were in their personalities, immensely.<br /><br />If you like unreliable narrators, cons, plot twists, political intrigue, character development, mythology, stories within stories, strong female characters and heart-warming romance and above all, a male protagonist that is all kinds of awesome, you should look no further than this series. It is not a perfect series by any means – there is change in pacing from one book to another, and the first book is clearly for a younger audience than the other two books. This is why, in my opinion, they should be read as a collection of books and not individually. I still love them though, flaws and all.<br /><br />At the end of book three, Eugenides has stolen: a gift; a man; a woman; peace; a kindgom. He has also stolen my heart.<br /><br />___________<br /><br />I know how cryptic this overview has been and that I did not provide any real details about the story. I still think you should find them out by yourself by reading the books, but if you want to know more you can read these reviews:<br /><br />Angieville’s: The Thief, The Queen of Attolia, The King of Attolia<br /><br />One last word: book 4 in the series, A Conspiracy of Kings is coming out in 2010. It is safe to say it my most anticipated book for 2010 along with The Wise Man’s Fear by Patrick Rothfuss.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18394080246783688358" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1859592058" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9208432961863962867">This has been on my TBR for over 2 years. Thank god I finally found time to dive into this series!<br/><br/><i>The Thief</i> is the first book of <i>The Queen's Thief</i> series. In it, you will meet Gen. Now he's a skilled thief and he can get himself in and out of anything. Well, not prison. However, the details about that situation aren't necessary because he has been chosen for a mission by the King himself. He has to go get a secret, but special, treasure and bring it back. <br/><br/>Now at this point, I'm thinking about so</span>
  <span id="freeText9208432961863962867" style="display:none">This has been on my TBR for over 2 years. Thank god I finally found time to dive into this series!<br /><br /><i>The Thief</i> is the first book of <i>The Queen's Thief</i> series. In it, you will meet Gen. Now he's a skilled thief and he can get himself in and out of anything. Well, not prison. However, the details about that situation aren't necessary because he has been chosen for a mission by the King himself. He has to go get a secret, but special, treasure and bring it back. <br /><br />Now at this point, I'm thinking about so many books or even a fairy tale or two that sound like this book. I will admit, it also made me more intrigued to see how this was going to go. Back to Gen and his mission impossible, his goal in life is to be free. So he will not even hesitate to take on this little mission. No matter the cost - he just doesn't want to rot in jail anymore. <br /><br />Gen was so lovable. I loved his sarcasm because it spoke to me on a deeper level. It's also my first language. However, I feel like not a lot happened in this book - which is weird. It might have to deal with how slow the pacing was for me - and this was the audio. <br /><br />Other than Gen, who I can't wait to hopefully see in the next book, the worldbuilding seemed too much. It was amazing but I felt a little bored when I got too much information about a single thing. I hope that the next book will give me less information and more action.<br /><br />Overall, I'm still so happy that I dove into this and I can't wait for the next book.<br /></span>

          </span>

<div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground">Readers also enjoyed</h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent"><div class='bookCarousel'>
<div class='carouselRow' style='width: 3600px'>

<li class='cover' id='bookCover_12432220'>

<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('SuB73MSSNYvMMX2M/vHTpncxrpGKcniRGjbRGYgm+pq3vITe2KkerGsM5hio0P96XqJ2PLOYrRpatyddX6hv2Q==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ed0tl7pBesQhOWwAoud8gJYJ6sGCbRzhtyLqnZ8PY3qEgdKVpnpR44YE95T0xlBcv5oybLuHyWr3oxzZSIH2OQ==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer8400940534517983304">Megan Whalen Turner is the author of short stories and novels for children, teenagers and adults. She has won the LA Times Book Award for Young Adult LIterature, a Boston Globe/ Horn Book Honor and a Newbery Honor. She won the Mythopoeic Award and was shortlisted twice for the Andre Norton Award.</span>
